  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_1ff8ae75-f941-4066-968e-afd107542485'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer376514406345759596">Daughter of a controlling mother, Elizabeth finally let loose one night, drinking at a nightclub and allowing a strange man's seductive Russian accent lure her to a house on Lake Shore Drive. The events that followed changed her life forever. <br/><br/>Twelve years later, the woman known as Abigail Lowery lives on the outskirts of a small town in the Ozarks. A freelance programmer, </span>
  <span id="freeText376514406345759596" style="display:none">Daughter of a controlling mother, Elizabeth finally let loose one night, drinking at a nightclub and allowing a strange man's seductive Russian accent lure her to a house on Lake Shore Drive. The events that followed changed her life forever. <br /><br />Twelve years later, the woman known as Abigail Lowery lives on the outskirts of a small town in the Ozarks. A freelance programmer, she designs sophisticated security systems -- and supplements her own security with a fierce dog and an assortment of firearms. She keeps to herself, saying little, revealing nothing. But Abigail's reserve only intrigues police chief Brooks Gleason. Her logical mind, her secretive nature, and her unromantic viewpoints leave him fascinated but frustrated. He suspects that Abigail needs protection from something -- and that her elaborate defenses hide a story that must be revealed.<br /><br />With a quirky, unforgettable heroine and a pulse-pounding plotline, Nora Roberts presents a riveting new read that cements her place as today's most reliably entertaining thriller -- and will leave people hungering for more.</span>

    <a title="♡Karlyn P♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1131400-karlyn-p"><img alt="♡Karlyn P♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389996373p2/1131400.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317497856?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♡Karlyn P♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♡Karlyn P♡" href="/user/show/1131400-karlyn-p">♡Karlyn P♡</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1131400-karlyn-p?shelf=published-2012">published-2012</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317497856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16034695463744753681"><br/><b>Nora Roberts is BACK!!</b> OK, I know many of you didn’t realize she left, but over the last few years her newer books have not cut it for me.  I found several of her latest stories full of filler and irrelevant content, and the core stories suffered as a result.  But in <b>The Witness</b> the story was  tight, the characters interesting, the romance swoon worthy, and the suspense totally believable.  Everything tied together, just like a great story should!<br/><br/>I never thought romance suspense was Ms Roberts b</span>
  <span id="freeText16034695463744753681" style="display:none"><br /><b>Nora Roberts is BACK!!</b> OK, I know many of you didn’t realize she left, but over the last few years her newer books have not cut it for me.  I found several of her latest stories full of filler and irrelevant content, and the core stories suffered as a result.  But in <b>The Witness</b> the story was  tight, the characters interesting, the romance swoon worthy, and the suspense totally believable.  Everything tied together, just like a great story should!<br /><br />I never thought romance suspense was Ms Roberts best genre, but she nails it in The Witness.   The story is told in two parts.  At first as we learn about the events that lead Elizabeth Fitch into a witness protection system at age 16, and then it fast forwards twelve years later.  Elizabeth is now living as Abigail Lowery and trying her best to stay unnoticed.  But Brook Gleason, the new sheriff in town, becomes very curious about this mysterious lady and proceeds to turn her world upside down.<br /><br />The heroine Elizabeth Fitch/Abigail Lowery is such an unusual heroine type.  A genius daughter of a neurosurgeon, her entire life was mapped out for her.  In a fit of rebellion at age 16, she becomes a witness to a gruesome murder by a Russian mofia organization in Chicago.   Believing she can trust the system to protect her, she nearly loses everything.<br /><br />Brooks was also a smart cookie, and recognized signs that made him suspect Abigail is running from something.  When his charming but tenacious drive for information is combined with a meddling hippie free-loving mother,  Abigail slowly begins to trust him. <br /><br />There were so many facets to this story that stood out, it is hard to summarize them all.   Watching Abigail learn to trust, and therefore truly live her life for the first time was wonderful to read.  Brooks devotion to her was heartwarming, and their time together full of passion and heat.   <br /><br />The suspense was brilliantly done, and never felt over the top.  The book never suffers from bad-guy overload either, we get just enough to know they are there and what they are capable of doing, but the main focus is on Brook and Abigail staying safe. <br /><br />The ending was pitch perfect! Like I said, I didn’t think romance suspense was Ms Roberts best genre, but I am now eating my words. This was really well done.   I would have looooooooved a longer epilogue (about the size of this book, to be honest, but I know that is totally unrealistic.) I didn’t want to let these characters go.   I would have liked if it had one particular twist in the end, but in truth it would have made the ending less spectacular, so Ms Roberts ended everything perfectly. Warning – Spoiler about the ending! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I really wanted her mother to finally grow a heart and re-enter Abigail’s life.  When Abigail is in the hospital near the end of the book, I hoped her mother would come in wearing a scrub outfit and they’d reconnect.  All the way to the end I was hoping the mother had an explanation for her actions, but alas the woman had no maternal instincts in her. So the book ended perfectly, and my farcical hope of a mother-daughter reunion was not to be had. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br />I had the great pleasure of listening to this story on audio.  The reader (Julia Whelan) is simply fantastic. One of the best narrated books I’ve listened to in a long time.  </span>
  <a data-text-id="16034695463744753681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_472774616" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472774616" />
    <a title="Sal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14856434-sal"><img alt="Sal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1355665749p2/14856434.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/472774616?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sal" href="/user/show/14856434-sal">Sal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780749955113" href="/book/show/13604177-the-witness">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer472774616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15051256610347413120">Don't get me wrong. This book is great. But it could have been so much more.<br/><br/>Though I haven't read any other books by Nora Roberts, I know she's a romance writer, not crime, or thriller, but I couldn't help wishing this book was a crime/thriller. The set-up to the main plot was really really good, fascinating, but then the rest of the book never reaches that level again. <br/><br/>To be honest, I'm a bit mean giving this two stars, but on a comparative level to the books I would give three stars, it falls </span>
  <span id="freeText15051256610347413120" style="display:none">Don't get me wrong. This book is great. But it could have been so much more.<br /><br />Though I haven't read any other books by Nora Roberts, I know she's a romance writer, not crime, or thriller, but I couldn't help wishing this book was a crime/thriller. The set-up to the main plot was really really good, fascinating, but then the rest of the book never reaches that level again. <br /><br />To be honest, I'm a bit mean giving this two stars, but on a comparative level to the books I would give three stars, it falls a little bit flat.<br /><br />I was reading, reading, reading and when I finished, all I thought was, that's it? So many characters that weren't developed yet (the bad guys) and she didn't extend the plot any further, instead she just concentrated on the romance part. Which is understandable, because that's the genre she writes, but it left me feeling empty. This had the potential to be the new 'Girl With The Dragon Tattoo'! The main character has a photographic memory, she has a ridiculous IQ, she's socially inept, say hello to interesting character who is crying out for a more character development and a more intense plot! Now USE her! Actually to be honest, her character was a little unrealistic when she was young, and I found it a little hard to warm to her. When she grew up, her talents and a little of her personality struck a resemblance to Lisbeth Salander (not as hardcore, of course), but I'm not complaining, because that's one of my favourite heroines ever.<br /><br />I'm going on and on and making this book appear to be a bad book, but it isn't. Honestly, it's good. But I feel frustrated at the potential this book has, and this potential was never reached. Instead, it was like this: Terrific set up, intriguing characters, romance, romance, romance, everything solved within ten pages, the end, boom.<br /><br />Sigh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15051256610347413120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_619493662" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619493662" />
    <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict"><img alt="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551124421p2/10717098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619493662?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol [Goodreads Addict]" href="/user/show/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict">Carol [Goodreads Addict]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780425264768" href="/book/show/15810151-the-witness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10717098-carol-goodreads-addict?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619493662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7197509108055265880"><a href='http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/nr_zps082add22.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400519597i/9684755.jpg' alt=' photo nr_zps082add22.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Nora Roberts has always been THAT author for me. The author that you know no matter what mood you were in, her books would be just right. But for some unexplainable reason, I have not read one of her books in such a long time. So when I received The Witness as a gift from my wonderful friend, I dove right in. And, as sure as the sun rises in the East, the book was perfect in every way. <br/><br/>First, I want to introduce you to Elizabeth Fitch. She is the sixteen year old daughter of Dr. Susan L. Fit</span>
  <span id="freeText7197509108055265880" style="display:none"><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/nr_zps082add22.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400519597i/9684755.jpg" alt=" photo nr_zps082add22.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Nora Roberts has always been THAT author for me. The author that you know no matter what mood you were in, her books would be just right. But for some unexplainable reason, I have not read one of her books in such a long time. So when I received The Witness as a gift from my wonderful friend, I dove right in. And, as sure as the sun rises in the East, the book was perfect in every way. <br><br>First, I want to introduce you to Elizabeth Fitch. She is the sixteen year old daughter of Dr. Susan L. Fitch. Elizabeth was conceived through IVF, the donor carefully chosen for the ultimate intellect, looks and health. This fact was clearly stated to Elizabeth, time and time again. Her mother is emotionless and controlling. She guides every aspect of Elizabeth’s life, her education, clothes, nutrition, daily activities. Elizabeth is technically a genius with a photographic memory. At sixteen, she is in Harvard and her mother has her set to begin medical school. This is not what Elizabeth wants, though. But she has never disobeyed her mother, until THAT night.<br><br>Elizabeth and her mother have argued for the first time. After Dr. Fitch leaves for a medical convention, Elizabeth goes to a mall for the first time, shops, and runs into a girl she once knew in school. They come up with a plan for a crazy night out, using false ID’s, going to a club and hoping to meet cute guys. But, this night does not turn out the way it was supposed to. Elizabeth is a witness to a horrible crime. She is taken into protective custody but through another equally horrible set of circumstances, she is forced to run on her own.<br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/nr_zpse8e044ed.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400519598i/9684757.jpg" alt=" photo nr_zpse8e044ed.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Fast forward twelve years. Elizabeth has become Abigail Lowery. She is living in a small town in the Ozarks. She has found a place she loves. A place she would like to call home. But she knows she can’t stay. Still, though, she has put down roots here. She has planted a butterfly garden and vegetable garden. She keeps to herself. She’s known as a loner. But there is one person that would like to break through that protective shell and see who is underneath.<br><br><a href="http://s1302.photobucket.com/user/caroldh4/media/butterflygarden_zps57457afb.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400519597i/9684759.jpg" alt=" photo butterflygarden_zps57457afb.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Brooks Gleason is the town Chief of Police. And he is intrigued by Abigail. He keeps showing up at her house unannounced and breaking down her defenses. Eventually Abigail does give in, knowing that this is something that can’t last. But she has never experienced romance, love. Never dated. She has so much trouble expressing herself but the things she says are just so completely endearing. Her awkwardness and naivety make her adorable. I loved Brooks and Abigail together. They were exactly what each other needed. But, Brooks knows Abigail is hiding something. He wants her to trust him enough to let him in. And can Abigail dare to dream of a future with Brooks, in this lovely town? Does she have the courage to finally face her past and put it to rest?<br><br><b>
  <i>"I'm half in love with you and heading fast toward three-quarters."</i>
</b><br><br>I loved this book so much. No one can write suspense and romance together like Nora Roberts. You will fall in love with Elizabeth/Abigail and Brooks. And also with Brook’s family. This book will make you sigh, smile and also grip the arms of your chair a little tighter. It was simply a wonderful book. I hope you’ll give it a try. <br><br><b>
  <i>"To be held like this on a cool spring night by someone who cared. It was like a miracle, even for someone who didn't believe in them."</i>
</b><br></span>

<div id="review_328876490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/328876490" />
    <a title="Karen Bonilla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5592838-karen-bonilla"><img alt="Karen Bonilla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1317225836p2/5592838.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/328876490?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Bonilla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Bonilla" href="/user/show/5592838-karen-bonilla">Karen Bonilla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer328876490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1684372787882059133">WARNING*** Contains Spoilers. I'm a big fan of Nora Roberts but I'm not sure why people gave this book such rave reviews. This book started out with a bang. Elizabeth is a 16 year old genius rebelling against her cold,controlling mother. She meets up with a Russian mafia don and witnesses the brutal murder of a mafia henchman and her teenaged female friend. She ends up on the run for her life. Twelve years later, she moves to a small town and meets and falls in love with the local sheriff, Brook</span>
  <span id="freeText1684372787882059133" style="display:none">WARNING*** Contains Spoilers. I'm a big fan of Nora Roberts but I'm not sure why people gave this book such rave reviews. This book started out with a bang. Elizabeth is a 16 year old genius rebelling against her cold,controlling mother. She meets up with a Russian mafia don and witnesses the brutal murder of a mafia henchman and her teenaged female friend. She ends up on the run for her life. Twelve years later, she moves to a small town and meets and falls in love with the local sheriff, Brooks. Elizabeth's character comes across as the stereotypical genius who would never, in a million years, be able to blend in in any gathering that didn't involve Mensa members. Her speech is stilted and stiff. She is a recluse who somehow thought that her antisocial ways would not be noticed in a small, rural community. Her love interest, Brooks, comes across as a paragon of virtues. He's too good to be true and as boring as can be. There's no edge there, no feeling of passion or drive. After they meet, the majority of the book revolves around their relationship and Elizabeth's caution and security interests; the alarms that alert her when intruders(or visitors) come on her property, her possession of numerous handguns, the loyal and well trained guard dog. In addition, pages cover her hacking into FBI and mafia computers and using those tools to damage the mafia. To make it even duller, they deal with towns people and their issues. I kept expecting something to happen. I kept waiting for the mafia to discover where she was and come in with guns blazing. That never happened. Instead, the bad guys were taken down without any kind of fight and then the book was over. To me, this book just fizzled. It was boring and bland. There was no suspense, no drama, no passion. The characters were stereotypical and as flat as the storyline.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1684372787882059133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/252804296?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2011</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Romance fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=author-nora-roberts-jd-robb">author-nora-roberts-jd-robb</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer252804296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8963356387996687679">5 stars – Contemporary Romance/Romantic Suspense<br/><br/>It’s hard to deny the talent and mass appeal of Nora Roberts considering <b>The Witness</b> is her 200th book. I mean...wow! That is quite an impressive achievement and a boon for romance readers. I consider myself a fan of hers, and I especially loved her <i>Bride Quartet</i> series and the few J.D. Robb <i>In Death</i> books that I’ve read. Some of her books tend to be a little bit too generic and plain vanilla for my taste, but I occasionally enjoy their comfort lik</span>
  <span id="freeText8963356387996687679" style="display:none">5 stars – Contemporary Romance/Romantic Suspense<br /><br />It’s hard to deny the talent and mass appeal of Nora Roberts considering <b>The Witness</b> is her 200th book. I mean...wow! That is quite an impressive achievement and a boon for romance readers. I consider myself a fan of hers, and I especially loved her <i>Bride Quartet</i> series and the few J.D. Robb <i>In Death</i> books that I’ve read. Some of her books tend to be a little bit too generic and plain vanilla for my taste, but I occasionally enjoy their comfort like good old vanilla ice cream, even if it doesn’t make them all that memorable.<br /> <br /><b>The Witness</b> is one of the better NR books that I’ve read. It’s a great contemporary suspense with satisfying romance between an extraordinary heroine and a protective cop hero. Often I find that my reading enjoyment tends to hinge on my feelings about the hero, but this time it was primarily the unique, unforgettable heroine who made me like the book so much. <br /><br />I loved the heroine, Elizabeth/Liz, right from the start and my heart ached for her. It’s told in four parts/acts with the first involving her as a sixteen-year-old girl, and the ending of the first act (page 100 in the Hardcover edition) was intense, pulse-pounding, and emotionally distressing. I admired the strong, formidable, self-reliant woman she became. Abigail is a kick-ass survivor in hiding with so many interesting, veiled layers, and it’s impossible not to like her, especially when her social awkwardness and gruff loner persona make her unintentionally funny and glimpses of that vulnerable girl yearning for affection and normalcy are revealed. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The part where she methodically researched proper etiquette and social customs of a barbecue on the Internet just to prepare for a casual gathering with Brooks’s family cracked me up. Yet it was also a bit heartbreaking when she became so easily discomfited by routine social graces and niceties. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br />Police Chief Brooks Gleason is a great hero, and he’s pushy and unyielding in his pursuit of Abigail yet remarkably patient and understanding of her as well. And I couldn’t possibly forget to mention Abigail’s loyal friend and guard dog, Bert, since their relationship adds so much to the story. Bert definitely deserves top dog honors for favorite animal companion.<br /><br />My one complaint is that I wanted more from the epilogue, but otherwise I really enjoyed this. So kudos to Ms. Roberts for her notable 200th release! 5 stars!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8963356387996687679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1086678040?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ingie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ingie" href="/user/show/15589375-ingie">Ingie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/18401735-the-witness">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ingie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15589375-ingie?shelf=books-i-read-2015">books-i-read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15589375-ingie?shelf=romance-m-f-suspense">romance-m-f-suspense</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1086678040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4775885417965495700"><i>Written July 17, 2015</i><br/><br/><b>4 1/2 Stars - Fantastic listening and a good well told thrilling plot. I'm to be honest surprised, but this NR romance impressed me...much</b><br/><br/>I bought this <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts' title='Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nora Roberts</a> as an 16:18 hrs audiobook (narrated by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2939944.Julia_Whelan' title='Julia Whelan' rel='nofollow noopener'>Julia Whelan</a>) already back in March. I honestly thought I was finished and done with NB-books several years ago, but never say never. <br/><br/><i>The Witness</i> (from 2012) has got so many happy reviews, and was much appreciated by both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/822479344?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kathleen</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175221627?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heather</a> as an audiobook. Convinced by fr</span>
  <span id="freeText4775885417965495700" style="display:none"><i>Written July 17, 2015</i><br><br><b>4 1/2 Stars - Fantastic listening and a good well told thrilling plot. I'm to be honest surprised, but this NR romance impressed me...much</b><br><br>I bought this <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts" title="Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">Nora Roberts</a> as an 16:18 hrs audiobook (narrated by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2939944.Julia_Whelan" title="Julia Whelan" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Whelan</a>) already back in March. I honestly thought I was finished and done with NB-books several years ago, but never say never. <br><br><i>The Witness</i> (from 2012) has got so many happy reviews, and was much appreciated by both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/822479344?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathleen</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175221627?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Heather</a> as an audiobook. Convinced by friends, I wanted to give <i>The Wittness</i> and a NB novel a "second" chance. It's was time. <br><br><a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Stars/image.jpg2_zps0azoxreu.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1430073383i/14677459.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg2_zps0azoxreu.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Wow! Sixteen highly entertaining listening hours</b><br><i>The Wittness</i> was from the very first chapter nerve-tingling and breathlessly exciting. I was at once on my edge. This pretty clever storyplot —mainly about fear, revenge, cruelty... but also about to fit in, be a "normal" girl, be loved and to sincerely trust someone once again— really got me. <br><br><u>An EXTRA STAR for a fantastic audiobook narration</u>. I'm not sure this should had been such a winner for me just reading by myself. <br><br>**********************************************<br><br><i>Chicago some years ago...</i><br><br><b>Elizabeth Fitch</b> is a sixteen years old super intelligent girl with a very controlling mother who let loose one (..ONE single) night. A night that change her life for ever. Two cruel murders, one of her new friend. Guilty men, Russian ancestors that all belongs to the mob in <i>Chicago</i>. From that night is Elizabeth a hunted victim.... she is the witness. <br><blockquote>
<a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Diverse/image.jpg5_zpsbehxb4vl.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434310781i/15202226.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg5_zpsbehxb4vl.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>“Love doesn’t turn on and off like a light switch.” <br><br><a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/City%20and%20nature%20etc/mountain%20etc/image.jpg5_zpsq9fwb3sh.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437161177i/15544141.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg5_zpsq9fwb3sh.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</blockquote><br><i>In a small Arkansas town...</i><br><br><b>Years later is there a police chief, Brooks Gleason</b> who is intrigued by <b>Abigail Lowery</b>, the mysterious woman living outside town since a while. He just feel and strongly suspects that this "armed" woman, with a huge scary dog, needs protection from something. Our hero Brooks is a man who likes to protect. He takes good care of his citizens and he like to solve tricky puzzles. Especially when there is an beautiful woman to get to know. <br><br>**********************************************<br><br><b>Learning to live a "real" life...</b><br>This poor teen girl. Yes, it was a traumatic start. I just wished her a better life. Elizabeth's mom was a egocentric bitch (in the right word and meaning) without any ability to feel feelings for, or want to take tender care of, of her own young daughter. <br><br>The first part with teenage Elizabeth isn't that long and the main storyline starts the day Abigail meets Brooks. <br><br>What a funny heroine we get here. This very intelligent and kind of geeky woman was just so adorable charming when she discovered feelings, the "love-play" and relationships stuff... ~ Chuckling fun. I allways enjoy to read about a bit cheesy (nerd) characters. A female character who almost talks like a living encyclopedia (must be some combination of "letters"..). Like this heroine. So likeable and charming. <br><blockquote>
<a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Diverse/image.jpg5_zpsbehxb4vl.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434310781i/15202226.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg5_zpsbehxb4vl.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>“Studies show adolescent males often make decisions based on sex. Many fail to grow out of it.” <br><br><a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Bodypart/image.jpg2_zpson1amwmm.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437119742i/15540136.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg2_zpson1amwmm.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>“After weighing the pros and cons, I’ve decided sex with you would be mutually satisfying. You’re attractive and pleasant. And clean. You kiss very well, and while I’ve found that’s not always a reliable gauge for skill in bed, it often follows. If you’re agreeable, we can finish dinner, I’ll show you the greenhouse, then we can go in and have sex. I’m on birth control, but I would require you wear a condom.” <br><br><a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Diverse/image.jpg5_zpsbehxb4vl.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434310781i/15202226.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg5_zpsbehxb4vl.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</blockquote><br><b>...and this wonderful M.A.N. !!</b><br>This gorgeous man. ~ A dream hero with an upbringing in a big warm caring hippie family. A friendly, but righteous policeman who moved back to his small hometown when his father was getting older and a bit sick, and when his mother —and (married) sisters— needed him for nearer support. The kind of man most women wish for. You know the kind: big &amp; strong, wise, tender, funny, charming, loyal and faithful, and cozy kissable sexy. Drool-worthy!<br><br>I also mostly like novels or romances set in small nice places or towns. Stories including tales about local people, about sweet old ladies, nice old friends, a odd secretary, a lovely mom, some adorable cute dogs (like <i>Big Bert</i> and <i>Sunny's</i> new puppy - a gift from her thoughtful son), etc etc. <br><br>I like suspense stories with a lot of romance feeling there...<u>and</u> some steamy hot moments. ~ I actually got it all here. (Some small dance moves..)<br><blockquote>
<a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/City%20and%20nature%20etc/Flowers/image_zps68a209eb.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437066099i/15534087.jpg" alt=" photo image_zps68a209eb.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>‘She was happy, she realized, as she marked off her plot with string and stakes. Really happy. With spring, with work, with her home. With Brooks. Had she been really happy before? Surely there had been moments...’<br><br><a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Diverse/image.jpg5_zpsbehxb4vl.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434310781i/15202226.jpg" alt=" photo image.jpg5_zpsbehxb4vl.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</blockquote><br>Did our heroine get her revenge, was there a pretty clever solution? ~ Read or listen and discover. <br><br>**********************************************<br><br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2939944.Julia_Whelan" title="Julia Whelan" rel="nofollow noopener">Julia Whelan</a> (narrator) does it so amazing well</b>.<br>She just swept me away with a nail biting thrilling suspense romance (..a genre perfect for me this summer vacation week). Quite long book but well worth the time.<br><br>Recommended to you who also "left" Ms. Roberts to other readers (those with lesser "good" taste in their book choices, haha) years ago. ~ I crawl to the cross, it may be more NR soon.<br><br><b>I LIKE - surprising good (audio) stories extremely well narrated</b><br><br><br>****<br><i>I gifted the translated (yes there really are some romances in Swedish sometimes) paperback to my older (71) mom last xmas. She enjoyed it (and she lent it to my picky sister). A good sign, my mom is this genre (S / R - steamy but not erotica) fan. </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4775885417965495700" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5846932862380546590">Fantastic read featuring one of the best heroines I have seen in a long time. She was so smart and capable, it was fun to see her try to understand how to deal with the friendly people in her new hometown. The hero was such a great personality, he was funny and easy going but had endless patience to get through all of Abigail/Liz's barriers (which she had very good reasons for having).   <span id="freeText5846932862380546590" style="display:none">Fantastic read featuring one of the best heroines I have seen in a long time. She was so smart and capable, it was fun to see her try to understand how to deal with the friendly people in her new hometown. The hero was such a great personality, he was funny and easy going but had endless patience to get through all of Abigail/Liz's barriers (which she had very good reasons for having). I enjoyed all of this book, parts were very suspenseful and other parts were funny and engaging. Nora Roberts shines with her characterizations, she really brings the whole town to life and gives the leads and side characters distinctive personalities. Obviously I recommend this book if you enjoy contemporary romance or romantic suspense.<br /><br />I listened to this on audio and the narrator does a great job showing the heroine's personality in the reading and she even did the male parts well.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331217331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13472428478393117854">The Witness <br/><b>4 ½ Stars!</b><br/>Very enjoyable read by Nora Roberts. Being a huge fan of her In Death series, which she writes under the pseudonym of J D Robb, I wanted to give her other books a try. I found myself totally absorbed in this compelling and intriguing novel. From the exciting beginning, when Liz becomes a witness to a brutal crime, to her transformation into Abigail, loner and security expert, I was drawn to her character and circumstances. The town where she settles is full of interesting c</span>
  <span id="freeText13472428478393117854" style="display:none">The Witness <br /><b>4 ½ Stars!</b><br />Very enjoyable read by Nora Roberts. Being a huge fan of her In Death series, which she writes under the pseudonym of J D Robb, I wanted to give her other books a try. I found myself totally absorbed in this compelling and intriguing novel. From the exciting beginning, when Liz becomes a witness to a brutal crime, to her transformation into Abigail, loner and security expert, I was drawn to her character and circumstances. The town where she settles is full of interesting characters that added depth and emotion to the story. She is pursued by the easygoing, relentless police chief Brooks Gleason. He annoys her, but at the same time he unearths feelings in her that she never thought possible. Theirs is a relationship that forms slowly, as Brooks gains Abigail’s trust, then worms and finagles his way into her life. These interactions made for some very humorous moments, as Abigail is almost robotic in personality and Brooks is smooth and charming. The dialogue between the two of them is fantastic and plentiful. The romance that develops is sweet, and at times heated. I found it to be the perfect balance. There is also a secondary storyline that briefly involves Abigail, but Brooks and some of the townspeople are the main focus. The two plots intertwined quite nicely. In my mind I had predicted how the story would end, but the author surprised me with an unexpected twist. It was fitting. <br /><br />There was one other character who played a major role in the book and I feel is worth a mention, Abigail’s dog Bert. He was as much a part of the story as Brooks and Abigail, and I found myself looking forward to the parts of the book where he was present. <br /><br />My only issue came in the way of the epilogue. When I read an epilogue, I expect and look forward to an update of the characters and what has become of them and their lives. This epilogue served as just another chapter in the book, updated only hours from the exciting ending. With the turmoil that plagued Abigail’s life, I had hoped to see what the future held for her and Brooks, and I was somewhat disappointed. However I highly recommend this book, not only for fans of Nora Roberts, but for lovers of romantic suspense. <br /><br /><b>Narration-5 Stars!</b><br />I’ve just recently discovered the wonderful world of audio books, but from the few I’ve listened too, I find that some are books are best to be read from the written word, while others can be just as enjoyable, or even more so, when someone reads them to you. The Witness is one of those books. Julia Whelan’s smooth steady narration had me mesmerized, and fully captured my attention. She is a narrator that I will be looking for in my future audio reads. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_275612030" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/275612030" />
    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3282244-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277923282p2/3282244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/275612030?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/3282244-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=first-reads-arcs-won-a-copy">first-reads-arcs-won-a-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=fiction-vixen-reviews">fiction-vixen-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275612030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13071824956856824568">After thinking about it for a bit, I realized that it has been quite a while since I have read a new standalone book by <i>Nora Roberts</i>. It was a nice change. I have no problem reading about a group of friends or relatives in a trilogy, but it was nice to know that everyone I met in the book existed solely to enrich <i>this</i> book.<br/><br/>One thing I love about this author is the way she sets up the backstory. If you’re familiar with her work then you probably already know that she likes to cut her books into s</span>
  <span id="freeText13071824956856824568" style="display:none">After thinking about it for a bit, I realized that it has been quite a while since I have read a new standalone book by <i>Nora Roberts</i>. It was a nice change. I have no problem reading about a group of friends or relatives in a trilogy, but it was nice to know that everyone I met in the book existed solely to enrich <i>this</i> book.<br /><br />One thing I love about this author is the way she sets up the backstory. If you’re familiar with her work then you probably already know that she likes to cut her books into sections (or Acts) to show the progression of the characters’ journey, but if not…well, now you know. :) The first section (the first 100 pages or so) of <i>The Witness</i> showed the heroine’s past. I got so much more involved in the events than if I had just been told about what happened to her back then. I loved seeing all the details for myself and found that getting to know the heroine in the past made it easier for me to get over some of the issues I had with her character later. I know that sometimes too much focus on the past can detract from the present, but I have always loved this habit of NR’s and have never found that to be the case.<br /><br />I found the whole storyline to be unique and different. The heroine witnessed a crime when she was a teenager and was forced to change her identity because of it. Can you imagine having to change everything about yourself? Her family (no big loss honestly), her future plans, they were all wiped out like they were nothing. I really liked getting to see how she coped with the past and lived her life as an adult. It also added an interesting layer to the romance. Your whole life is a lie. How close do you get to someone when you factor that in? Do you tell your love interest the truth and risk exposing yourself? I liked that what kept them apart felt <i>real</i>. It wasn’t just some simple, manufactured reason, blown up to epic proportion to provide drama.<br /><br />I think that the heroine, Abigail (originally Elizabeth), was a great character, but she occasionally veered toward the cold end of things. I think she was supposed to be similar to Miranda from <i>Homeport</i> (Anyone read it? Great book!), given that they both processed things scientifically and logically and they were both rather socially awkward, but Miranda had a vulnerability to her that Abigail lacked. That lack of softness occasionally made it hard to connect with her. We knew she was scared due to the way she lived and her refusal to let people into her life, but I never really <i>felt</i> it from her. <br /><br />That’s one of the reasons that having that section of backstory really helped for me. I <i>did</i> feel the emotion and fear in the beginning, so I had that to draw on. I just think that in addition to the emotionless way she was raised, being on the run for so long removed her from the world so effectively that it was hard for even the reader to get close to her. I’m not sure if she was cast this way by design, but it kept me from fully sinking into her character and the relationship. That said, it didn’t keep me from enjoying the rest of the book.<br /><br />Brooks, the hero, is not delved into as deeply as Abigail was, but he was much easier to love. He’s amusing and charming and he does a wonderful job of loosening Abigail up. I thought it was cute that we first met him when he was sitting in the town’s café, positioned specifically to be able to see Abigail on the off chance that she would come to town to shop that day. He was interested in her, both as a cop and as a man, and he finally decided to take a chance and go chat her up, despite her ‘Leave me alone’ vibe. He was shot down, and he was shot down hard, but I’ve got to give him props for determination. He just kept bugging her, trying to charm her, until he eventually grew on her. Like mold. :P <br /><br />The small town was charming, but kept away from the hokey, cheesy characterization that always drives me nuts. Brooks had a lot more ties to the community than Abigail did, so we were given a better picture of the inhabitants when we were in his point of view. His family was fun to read about, especially his mom, and it was nice to see a lot of his job instead of just focusing on the suspense plot surrounding the heroine. <br /><br />One thing that I found odd about the story, but that I liked more and more upon further reflection, was the suspense plot. Truthfully, it wasn’t very suspenseful. The heroine had her life turned upside down by a murder, yes, but there was no menacing presence breathing down her neck like you usually see in an RS. She changed her identity and was <i>very</i> prepared for possible discovery, but that was all a background feature. When the end resolution came, we were told about it more than it was shown. At first that bothered me because I wanted a seat at the front lines, you know? But the more I thought about it the more I realized that the book wasn’t set up to play out like the usual Suspense story. She played her part and she moved on. She didn’t need be a witness for it to be over for her. If you’re looking for an RS that’s heavy on the suspense, this isn’t that book. Just an FYI for you. <br /><br /><b>Favorite Quote:</b><br /><blockquote>So far the only strike against me is curiosity?”<br /><br />“There are others. Proximity, for one, which would make it awkward and problematic when I no longer want to have sex with you.”<br /><br />“What makes you think you’re going to want to stop having sex with me?”<br /><br />She got out two glasses, two small plates, two forks. “The law of averages.”<br /><br />“Oh, that. I defy averages.”<br /><br />“A lot of people believe they do. They don’t.”</blockquote> <br /><b>*Review originally posted on <a href="http://www.fictionvixen.com/2012/04/review-the-witness-by-nora-roberts.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Fiction Vixen</a>*</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13071824956856824568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_639571447" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/639571447" />
    <a title="Foxfire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312002-foxfire"><img alt="Foxfire" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/639571447?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Foxfire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Foxfire" href="/user/show/5312002-foxfire">Foxfire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer639571447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13155543775487301509">DNF for me. I loved the first 25% where the young Elizabeth breaks free from her controlling mother and witnesses a murder.<br/><br/>The next section shows her 12 years later, living a life in hiding. This is where the story fell apart for me.<br/> <br/>1. After 2-3 brief conversations, Elizabeth, a recluse who avoids all human contact, and Brooks, a police chief on duty, engage in bold banter about whether to have sex or not. I felt this was totally out of character and unrealistic.<br/><br/>2. In the next scene, we get the</span>
  <span id="freeText13155543775487301509" style="display:none">DNF for me. I loved the first 25% where the young Elizabeth breaks free from her controlling mother and witnesses a murder.<br /><br />The next section shows her 12 years later, living a life in hiding. This is where the story fell apart for me.<br /> <br />1. After 2-3 brief conversations, Elizabeth, a recluse who avoids all human contact, and Brooks, a police chief on duty, engage in bold banter about whether to have sex or not. I felt this was totally out of character and unrealistic.<br /><br />2. In the next scene, we get the clichéd Other Woman. The other woman is usually a beautiful blonde, and she is either a bitchy ex-wife, or a clinging ex-girlfriend who won't let go. In this case it's the clinging ex-girlfriend. I hate the beautiful blonde cliché. Being blond and beautiful does not make a woman evil.<br /><br />3. In the next few scenes, we have the hero rejecting the advances of the clinging ex. Then he goes off to the heroine and gives her a detailed rundown of his sexual history with the ex, including a description of how he turned her down - because he'd rather sleep with the heroine. To me, this is blatant kiss-and-tell. An honourable man does not belittle and humiliate one woman in order to seduce another. The hero is behaving like a sleazebag.<br /><br />4. The hero and heroine go to bed and have athletic sex. Here I'm totally lost about the heroine's character. She avoids all social contact, except a trip to a grocery store when necessary. She never lets anyone into her house, and she never goes out unarmed. And yet we are expected to believe that she likes to have sex and has done it with some frequency with strangers. Whoa? Would a woman afraid of any situation that makes her physically vulnerable just go off and have sex, a situation which makes a person more defenceless, less able to respond to a sudden attack, than almost any other circumstance?<br /><br />Further, it just does not make sense how Elizabeth keeps saying she wants to be normal. Yes, she has genius IQ and was brought up by a controlling mother, and she experienced a trauma and perceives herself under threat, but since seventeen she has been in charge of her life and if she really wanted to, she could live much more normally. <br /><br />Since seventeen, she has watched popular TV and movies. She went to college, which means she's had plenty of exposure to young people. She surfs the web, can visit chat rooms, learn how people talk. She is highly intelligent. She has the skills to blend in, to appear ordinary - which she claims to be her main objective - and yet she talks like a science textbook and lives in a way which is guaranteed to draw attention to her. Moreover, the minute she starts talking to someone, she tells them how extraordinary she is. It just does not make sense.<br /><br />That's what killed the book for me. The character of heroine is not credible at all. Which is a real shame, because it was a great story idea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13155543775487301509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_313927031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313927031" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313927031?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duchess Nicole" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole">Duchess Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-romantic-suspense">genre-romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-contemp-romance">genre-contemp-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313927031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14526949377114849857">While this book took a loooong time to get set up, even the setup part was really good. Elizabeth rebels against her robot Mom (she's not really a robot, but the lady doesn't hug, wear color, or do anything without a schedule) when she's sixteen. That's what teenagers do, and even though Liz is a bit of a mini-robot, she's still a teenager girl who wants to live her own life, not the one her 'mother' picks for her. <br/><br/>This one decision leads to the witnessing of a horrible crime committed by a crim</span>
  <span id="freeText14526949377114849857" style="display:none">While this book took a loooong time to get set up, even the setup part was really good. Elizabeth rebels against her robot Mom (she's not really a robot, but the lady doesn't hug, wear color, or do anything without a schedule) when she's sixteen. That's what teenagers do, and even though Liz is a bit of a mini-robot, she's still a teenager girl who wants to live her own life, not the one her 'mother' picks for her. <br /><br />This one decision leads to the witnessing of a horrible crime committed by a crime family with far-reaching influence. So Liz has to rely on her brilliant mind to hide herself from not only the bad guys, but the good guys as well. <br /><br />Fast forward over a decade, and Abigail Lowry is a practical hermit, living in self imposed solitude in her cabin near a small town in the middle of nowhere. She just wants to be left alone with her genius self, hiding from the world behind her ridiculously modern security system and faithful guard dog, Bert. (It IS Nora Roberts, you know there has to be a dog) Not only is she still in hiding, but she's so socially inept that just her oddity gets tongues wagging whenever she goes to the supermarket. Small towns are not a good place to hide, Abigail!!<br /><br />She quickly catches the eye of the local police chief, Brooks Gleason. Their relationship builds slowly, and what a sweet couple they turn out to be! Brooks is so patient with Abigail. He thinks her oddities are cute; in fact, I do believe her rigidity and need for order was a turn on for the sexy, laid back chief! Bert the dog was an endearing character in his own right, and just reiterates how the loyalty and love shown by our canine family members is one fabulous gift from God. Want unconditional love? Screw a boyfriend/husband. Get a dog!<br /><br />The suspense is offset by the love story between Brooks and Abigail and I just loved it! The only thing that I didn't love is the abrupt ending frequently mentioned by other reviewers. The bad guy's comeuppance is alluded to, but after reading this very long book, I needed more of an eff you that what I got. These guys are organized crime, doing atrocious things....they needed at least a few more pages of detailed revenge taken out on them. <br /><br />Again, we got another gem from the master who is Nora Roberts! I'm the biggest cliche in the reading world when I say she is one of my favorite authors, but the lady is flat out talented, and turns them out like none other. This was her 200th book, folks! Crazy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14526949377114849857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_345211787" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/345211787" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/345211787?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9781455886883" href="/book/show/14594870-the-witness">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of analytical, smart heroines matched with laid back heroes</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to  Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1802746-shawna">Shawna</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=russian-storyline-or-characters">russian-storyline-or-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2013-200s-club-challenge">2013-200s-club-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=yearly-reading-challenge-2013">yearly-reading-challenge-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=nerd-prof-scientist-genius-geek">nerd-prof-scientist-genius-geek</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=kickbutt-heroine">kickbutt-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-falls-hard-for-heroine-fast">hero-falls-hard-for-heroine-fast</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-i-liked">hero-i-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-liked">heroine-i-liked</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer345211787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer578089315707231212">I want to thank Shawna for recommending this book to me. In all honesty, I am not a huge fan of Nora Roberts' romance novels, although I do like her JD Robb In Death series. While this book didn't change my opinion of her on convert her to a must-read author for me, I enjoyed this book, and I can see she is a very good writer. Having said that, I don't find her romance style very moving personally. As far as suspense, she definitely works better for me. <br/><br/>This novel feels like an odyssey. It start</span>
  <span id="freeText578089315707231212" style="display:none">I want to thank Shawna for recommending this book to me. In all honesty, I am not a huge fan of Nora Roberts' romance novels, although I do like her JD Robb In Death series. While this book didn't change my opinion of her on convert her to a must-read author for me, I enjoyed this book, and I can see she is a very good writer. Having said that, I don't find her romance style very moving personally. As far as suspense, she definitely works better for me. <br /><br />This novel feels like an odyssey. It starts with a very young, innocent teenage girl whose rigidly structured, emotionally vacant life is completely destroyed by one bad decision she makes out of rebellion. Nora Roberts invests us in the emotional and intellectual journey of this young woman, and I completely felt for and loved young Elizabeth. This was highly crucial to go back to when things went pear-shaped so that we could relate to the older version of this character, who is now living as Abigail Lowery.<br /><br />What didn't work quite as well as the diversion that the storyline takes with the Blake family and their out-of-control son. While this was more germane to Brooks Gleason's (Abigail's love interest) narrative, I don't think it really tied very well into the main plot of Abigail, what and who she was running from, and I'm not sure it was that important to Brooks' characterization. Even at the end, I wasn't convinced that it was necessary to the story. More than anything, it was just added local color. <br /><br />The romance part mostly worked for me, but it didn't set the page on fire. Roberts idea of romance just isn't dramatic enough for me. Even the sensual scenes didn't have much spark for me. I could see the love between Abigail and Brooks, and I really liked how Brooks was willing to be there for her and to be whatever she needed him to be. Although at the same time, Brooks could be quite obstinate and set in his ways kind of guy and forceful (in an aww-shucks, disarming but I'm a brickwall manner) about getting his way in situations. He was like a immovable mountain about some things, and Abigail had to be the one who changed her viewpoint in those areas. It was funny and kind of cute how he pushed Abigail out of her unemotional/controlled, Fortress of Solitude mien and left her completely discombobulated. I can see their marriage being very interesting, considering the way their personalities are so different. Where Abigail is the analytical, rule-oriented person, Brooks is very instinctive, and emotional. At the same time, he's a very steady guy who you know you can trust. That's highly appealing. I do feel like they were able to meet each other halfway and didn't steamroll each other, which was good. So I could believe they were a perfect match.<br /><br />Ultimately, what I loved most of all is how Brooks was perfectly fine with earning his way in Abigail's insular life by letting his actions show he was trustworthy and that deserved her love. He also didn't try to take away Abigail's need to make decisions and autonomy in her life, because he knew how important that was. Sometimes, I imagine it was hard for him not to take it personally, but he looked past his own feelings to the whys and was willing to give her that and support her on things she really needed. <br /><br />As for Abigail, I think loving Brooks helped her to grow in crucial ways. For her to know it was okay not to understand the rules for everything, and to just go with the flow emotionally in relationships that were based on mutual trust. I think the O'Hara/Gleason clan will be good for Abigail, but I think I would find them overwhelming at times. They are quite pushy! I can't imagine Abigail not feeling that way based on her previous familial frame of reference.<br /><br />The Volkov storyline was very intriguing, but I was left feeling a little disappointed at the conclusion. The resolution made sense, but I was hoping for a more face to face confrontation. I guess that's the action/drama hound in me. I guess that was the best way to handle it, but man I would have loved some buttkicking and a show off. Abigail was kind of a bad@$$, but she never got to show it. Oh well.<br /><br />Overall, this was a good read.<br /><br /><b>Things I loved</b>:<br /><br />*Such a brilliant, analytical, heroine <br />*Brooks' laid back, but Bulldoggedly stubborn personality and his southern charm.<br />*The descriptions and imagery built by Roberts writing.<br />*Russian mafia storyline and how Abigail continually gets one over on them<br />*Crazy O'Hara/Gleason family dynamics--like watching reality tv<br />*Abigail's dog Bert<br />*Small town slice of life<br /><br />Worth a <b>4.25/5.0 star</b> rating. I'd recommend it.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="578089315707231212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30575403-lizzy?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30575403-lizzy?shelf=stars-3">stars-3</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30575403-lizzy?shelf=00-next-books">00-next-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1234991984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8124232098100294872"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12716613.The_Witness' title='The Witness by Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Witness</a> is a great entertainment. There is a controlling mother, murder and a teenager-witness, corruption, betrayal, hiding under an alias and building a new life, constant fear of discovery and romance (it’s a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/625.Nora_Roberts' title='Nora Roberts' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nora Roberts</a> book, after all). If you are looking for some angst and thrilling moments, it might be just the pick for you. </span>
  <span id="freeText8124232098100294872" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12716613.The_Witness" title="The Witness by Nora Roberts" rel="nofollow noopener">The Witness</a> is a great entertainment. If you are looking for some angst and thrilling moments, it might be just the pick for you. </span>
